</span><span class="cl-9d45c09e">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9d460ebf"><p class="cl-9d45d20a"><span class="cl-9d45c09e">368.4</span></p></td><td concentrated near their border, each side claiming it was part of routine military exercises in the area.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9d7935c8"><p class="cl-9d79040e"><span </span><span class="cl-9d78f86a">in</span><span class="cl-9d78f86a"> </span><span class="cl-9d78f86a">this</span><span class="cl-9d78f86a"> </span><span class="cl-9d78f86a">sentence</span><span "tremendous concern" over the continuing massing of Pakistani troops along the border; but he added that India was always willing to discuss the situation with Pakistan to solve their problems.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9d7935c8"><p class="cl-9d79040e"><span class="cl-9d78f86a">India</span><span class="cl-9d78f860"> </span><span class="cl-9d78f860">initiated</span><span </span><span class="cl-9d78f860">initiated</span><span class="cl-9d78f860"> </span><span class="cl-9d78f86a">disapprove</span><span class="cl-9d78f860"> </span><span the Indian navy was asked to "keep its eyes open."</span></p></td><td class="cl-9d7935c8"><p class="cl-9d79040e"><span class="cl-9d78f860">No</span><span class="cl-9d78f860"> </span><span withdrawal, sector-by-sector, to end the military confrontation within 15 days.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9d7935d3"><p class="cl-9d79040e"><span class="cl-9d78f860">No</span><span along the border.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9d7935c8"><p class="cl-9d79040e"><span class="cl-9d78f860">No</span><span class="cl-9d78f860"> </span><span border with Pakistan.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9d7935d3"><p class="cl-9d79040e"><span class="cl-9d78f860">No</span><span class="cl-9d78f860"> </span><span </span><span class="cl-9d9930f8">a</span><span class="cl-9d9930f8"> </span><span class="cl-9d99310c">start</span><span class="cl-9d99310c"> </span><span class="cl-9d99310c">of</span><span class="cl-9db40da6">On 24 September Nigeria's Chief of Army Staff, Major-General Abacha, visited Cameroon -- to affirm the "commitment of Nigeria toward peace and progress and toward the stability and peaceful coexistence between Cameroon and Nigeria."</span></p></td><td class="cl-9db43c9a"><p class="cl-9db41954"><span class="cl-9db40dc4">Nigeria</span><span class="cl-9db40da6"> </span><span </span><span class="cl-9db40dc4">sentence</span><span class="cl-9db40dc4"> </span><span class="cl-9db40dc4">7</span><span class="cl-9db40da6">.</span></p></td></tr><tr </span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">Africa</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">initiated</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">However, it did not impose economic sanctions on Pretoria.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d603"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">No</span><span Africa.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">No</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr </span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">act</span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">in</span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">this</span><span class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">Serious clashes between the SADF and Angolan forces continued intermittently for months, intertwined with the ongoing civil war in Angola between the MPLA-led government and UNITA.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">Angola</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">Angola</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">initiated</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span first time that his troops were fighting alongside UNITA inside Angola.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">South</span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">Africa</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">initiated</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">accept</span><span which recommended 1 November 1988 to the UN Secretary-General as the date for the implementation of Resolution 435, set 1 September as the date to resolve any other underlying issues and the date by which South Africa must be fully out of Angola, prepared text for a trilateral treaty that would make the New York Principles binding, and created an effective end to the Angolan border South Africa's military incursion into Angola.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">No</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd0d603"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">More forceful Security Council action, notably economic sanctions, was prevented by the threat of a U.S. veto.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d603"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">No</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9dd0d602"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">380.23</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">For years the Reagan administration had provided South Africa and UNITA with covert aid.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">No</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9dd0d60c"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">380.24</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d603"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">Moreover, its policy of "constructive engagement" with Pretoria included preventing any sanctions by the global organization.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d603"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">No</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9dd0d602"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">380.25</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">Complementing this policy, U.S. relations with Angola had steadily deteriorated after July 1985, when the U.S. Congress repealed the Clark Amendment, which had imposed legal restrictions on U.S. assistance to UNITA. Export credit funds to Angola were cut off.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">No</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9dd0d60c"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">380.26</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d603"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">And pressure was put on U.S. oil firms to cease their operations in oil-rich Angola, so as to deny funds to the pro-Soviet MPLA-led Angolan government.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d603"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">No</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9dd0d602"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">380.27</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">Both the USSR and Cuba, as noted, provided substantial military aid to government forces.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">No</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9dd0d60c"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">380.28</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d603"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">(South Africa Intervention in Angola was the last international crisis of the Angola protracted conflict: the December 1988 accord was fully implemented by Angola, Cuba, and South Africa.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d603"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">South</span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">Africa</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">initiated</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">withdraw</span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">from</span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">area</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">toward</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">Angola</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9dd0d602"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">380.29</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">And with the active involvement of the U.S., Russia, and South Africa, Namibia's independence became a reality in 1990.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">Namibia</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">initiated</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">political</span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">succession</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">toward</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">South</span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">Africa</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9dd0d60c"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">380.30</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d603"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">There were several abortive peace agreements over the years, notably the Angola Peace Accords on 31 May 1991, and the UN-supervised elections in September 1992.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d603"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">No</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9dd0d602"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">380.31</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">The electoral outcome, a decisive MPLA victory, was rejected by UNITA, and large-scale violence was renewed.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">No</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9dd0d60c"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">380.32</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d603"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">However, the 20-year-old civil war, the primary source of the Angola PC and its international crises, appeared to be winding down.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d603"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">No</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td Protocol, was signed in November 1994 between the MPLA-dominated government of Angola and the UNITA movement.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">toward</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f8a">Angola</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td Savimbi, had a public reconciliation in Lusaka in early May 1995, their first meeting since the ill-fated UN-organized Angola elections in 1992.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d603"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">No</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9dd0d602"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">380.35</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">After further negotiations, Angola's president announced in August 1995 that they had agreed to a merger -- and large-scale demobilization -- of their armed forces, as well as the formation of a coalition government in which Savimbi would serve as Vice President.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">No</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd0d603"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">But the deadline for the UN-sponsored demobilization, 8 February 1996, passed with little progress in this crucial domain of the Lusaka peace process.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d603"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">No</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">Still another agreement between dos Santos and Savimbi was reported at a meeting in Libreville, the capital of Gabon, on 1 March 1996.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">No</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr </span><span class="cl-9dd08f76">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9dd0d602"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">380.39</span></p></td><td with the assumption of ministerial posts by UNITA, including the vice presidency by Savimbi -- as provided in the Accord.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d5f8"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span resolved).</span></p></td><td class="cl-9dd0d60d"><p class="cl-9dd09cc8"><span class="cl-9dd08f76">No</span><span class="cl-9dd08f76"> </span><span
